# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--v11.4.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--v11.4.0$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Onboarding: Grafana Codebase Orientation

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/grafana--v11.4.0 (mirror of grafana/grafana)
**Task Type:** Codebase Orientation (analysis only — no code changes)

## Scenario

You are a new platform engineer joining the Grafana team. Your first task is to understand the codebase architecture — how the Go backend, React frontend, plugin system, and provisioning pipeline fit together. The codebase is large (~1.4GB, mixed Go/TypeScript/React), so targeted exploration is essential.

## Your Task

Explore the Grafana codebase and answer the following questions. Write your answers to `/logs/agent/onboarding.md`.

### 1. Main Entry Points
Where is the main server binary entry point? What CLI framework does Grafana use? How does the server bootstrap (what services/registries are initialized at startup)?

### 2. Core Backend Packages
Name at least 5 key Go packages under `pkg/` and describe their responsibilities. Include: API routing, service registry, data source proxy, alerting, and authentication.

### 3. Datasource Plugin Architecture
How does Grafana's plugin system work? Where are built-in datasource plugins defined? How does the backend communicate with plugin processes (gRPC, HTTP)? What is the role of the `grafana-plugin-sdk-go`?

### 4. Dashboard Provisioning Pipeline
Trace how a dashboard defined in a YAML provisioning file gets loaded into Grafana. What is the provisioning service? Where are provisioning configs read from? How do they get persisted to the database?

### 5. Frontend Build System
What frontend framework and build tools does Grafana use? How is the React frontend organized (packages, workspace structure)? Where is the main frontend entry point?

### 6. Extension: Adding a New Panel Plugin
If you needed to add a new visualization panel plugin, what steps would be needed? Which directories and configuration files would you touch? How does the plugin registry discover new panels?

## Output Requirements

Write a markdown document to `/logs/agent/onboarding.md` with numbered sections (1-6) matching the questions above. For each section:
- Be specific: include file paths, package names, function names
- Cite the actual code — reference specific files you explored
- Keep each section focused (2-4 paragraphs)

## Constraints

- Do NOT modify any source files
- Exploration and documentation only
- Be specific — include file paths, package names, function names

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive onboarding document at `/logs/agent/onboarding.md` that covers all 6 required sections with detailed architecture information.

## Summary of the Onboarding Document

The document provides a complete architectural overview of Grafana v11.4.0:

### **1. Main Entry Points**
- Binary entry: `pkg/cmd/grafana/main.go` using urfave/cli v2
- Bootstrap via `server.Initialize()` with Google Wire DI
- Signal handling for graceful shutdown

### **2. Core Backend Packages**
Identified and documented 6 key packages:
- `pkg/api`: HTTP API routing (50+ endpoints)
- `pkg/services/datasources`: Data source management
- `pkg/tsdb`: Built-in datasource drivers (Prometheus, Loki, Elasticsearch, CloudWatch, etc.)
- `pkg/services/provisioning`: YAML-based configuration pipeline
- `pkg/services/auth*`: Authentication and authorization
- `pkg/registry`: Service registration pattern

### **3. Datasource Plugin Architecture**
- Plugin system with in-memory registry
- Uses `grafana-plugin-sdk-go/backend` interfaces
- Built-in datasources follow standard pattern
- External plugins communicate via HTTP proxy

### **4. Dashboard Provisioning Pipeline**
- Reads YAML from `provisioning/dashboards/`
- File discovery and polling for changes
- Syncs to database via `DashboardProvisioningService`
- Orphaned dashboard cleanup

### **5. Frontend Build System**
- React + TypeScript with Webpack
- NX/Lerna monorepo with 11+ packages
- Entry point: `public/app/index.ts`
- Structured into core, features, plugins, store, routes

### **6. Adding a New Panel Plugin**
- Step-by-step guide with configuration requirements
- Frontend component pattern
- Backend support options
- Plugin discovery mechanism

The application uses the **urfave/cli v2** framework for command-line parsing and routing.\n\n**Bootstrap Flow:**\n1. The grafana-server command delegates to the main `grafana` binary via `pkg/util/cmd/cmd.go:RunGrafanaCmd()` (lines 15-74)\n2. The main CLI app is created in `pkg/cmd/grafana/main.go:MainApp()` (lines 34-73), which registers two CLI commands:\n   - `CLICommand`: For grafana-cli utilities\n   - `ServerCommand`: For starting the server\n\n3. The server command is defined in `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go:ServerCommand()` (lines 28-44)\n4. The `RunServer()` function (lines 46-125) performs the bootstrap:\n   - Reads configuration from `setting.NewCfgFromArgs()` (lines 96-101)\n   - Initializes profiling and tracing (lines 71-76)\n   - Calls `server.Initialize()` from `pkg/server/server.go` (lines 108-120)\n   - Sets up signal handling for graceful shutdown (line 123)\n   - Runs the HTTP server (line 124)\n\n### Service Initialization\nThe `server.Initialize()` function uses **Google Wire** dependency injection (defined in `pkg/server/wire.go`) to instantiate all core services. The Wire configuration includes 50+ services covering APIs, datasources, authentication, provisioning, and more (wire.go lines 39-443).\n\n## 2. Core Backend Packages\n\nGrafana's backend architecture is organized under `pkg/` with the following key packages:\n\n### 1. **pkg/api** - HTTP API and Routing\n- **Location**: `pkg/api/api.go` (HTTP routes registered at line 55)\n- **Responsibility**: Defines REST API endpoints, middleware, and request handlers\n- **Key Files**:\n  - `http_server.go`: HTTPServer struct and initialization\n  - `routing/`: Route registration and matching logic\n  - Handlers for dashboards, datasources, folders, users, plugins, etc.\n- **Pattern**: Each resource type has a handler file (e.g., `dashboard.go`, `datasources.go`)\n\n### 2. **pkg/services/datasources** - Data Source Management\n- **Location**: `pkg/services/datasources/`\n- **Responsibility**: Data source CRUD operations, caching, and service proxy\n- **Key Components**:\n  - `service/`: Main datasource service with cache implementation\n  - Integrates with `pkg/tsdb/` for backend plugin communication\n\n### 3. **pkg/tsdb** - Time Series Database Plugins\n- **Location**: `pkg/tsdb/`\n- **Responsibility**: Built-in data source drivers\n- **Built-in Datasources** (examples):\n  - `prometheus/`: Prometheus datasource (pkg/tsdb/prometheus/prometheus.go)\n  - `loki/`: Loki logs datasource\n  - `elasticsearch/`: Elasticsearch datasource\n  - `cloudwatch/`, `azuremonitor/`, `cloud-monitoring/`: Cloud integrations\n- **Pattern**: Each datasource implements the `backend.QueryDataHandler`, `backend.CheckHealthHandler`, and `backend.CallResourceHandler` interfaces from `grafana-plugin-sdk-go`\n\n### 4. **pkg/services/provisioning** - Configuration Provisioning\n- **Location**: `pkg/services/provisioning/`\n- **Responsibility**: Loads dashboards, datasources, plugins, and alerting rules from YAML files\n- **Key Components**:\n  - `provisioning.go` (lines 39-88): Main ProvisioningService\n  - `dashboards/`: Dashboard provisioning (reads YAML, syncs to DB)\n  - `datasources/`: Datasource provisioning\n  - `plugins/`: Plugin provisioning\n\n### 5. **pkg/services/authentication & Authorization**\n- **Location**: `pkg/services/auth/`, `pkg/services/authn/`, `pkg/services/accesscontrol/`\n- **Responsibility**: User authentication, identity providers, RBAC\n- **Components**:\n  - `auth/idimpl/`: ID token service\n  - `authn/authnimpl/`: Authentication service (supports OAuth, LDAP, SAML)\n  - `accesscontrol/acimpl/`: Access control and permission evaluation\n\n### 6. **pkg/registry** - Service Registry\n- **Location**: `pkg/registry/`\n- **Responsibility**: Registry pattern for discovering and registering background services\n- **Key Interfaces**:\n  - `BackgroundServiceRegistry`: Services that run in the background\n  - `UsageStatsProvidersRegistry`: Providers for usage statistics\n\n## 3. Datasource Plugin Architecture\n\n### Plugin System Overview\nGrafana supports two types of plugins:\n1. **Built-in datasources**: Compiled into the binary (under `pkg/tsdb/`)\n2. **Plugin datasources**: External processes communicating via gRPC or HTTP\n\n### Plugin Structure\n**Plugin Metadata** (`plugin.json`):\n- Located in `pkg/plugins/plugins.go:JSONData` (lines 87-100)\n- Defines plugin ID, type, name, category, and routing\n\n**Plugin Registry**:\n- Located in `pkg/plugins/manager/registry/in_memory.go`\n- In-memory registry stores all loaded plugins\n- Plugins registered via `registry.Add()` (lines 45-58)\n- Query plugins via `registry.Plugin()` (lines 29-31)\n\n### Backend Plugin Communication\n**grafana-plugin-sdk-go**:\n- Grafana uses `github.com/grafana/grafana-plugin-sdk-go/backend` interface\n- Built-in datasources implement these handlers:\n  - `QueryDataHandler`: Execute queries\n  - `CheckHealthHandler`: Health checks\n  - `CallResourceHandler`: Custom resource endpoints\n  - `AdmissionHandler`: Validate/mutate objects\n  - `StreamHandler`: Real-time streaming\n  - `CollectMetricsHandler`: Prometheus metrics\n\n**Example: Prometheus Datasource** (`pkg/tsdb/prometheus/prometheus.go`):\n```go\nfunc (s *Service) QueryData(ctx context.Context, req *backend.QueryDataRequest) (*backend.QueryDataResponse, error)\nfunc (s *Service) CheckHealth(ctx context.Context, req *backend.CheckHealthRequest) (*backend.CheckHealthResult, error)\n```\n\n### Plugin Loading\n**Plugin Manager**: `pkg/plugins/manager/`\n- `loader/loader.go`: Discovers and loads plugins from disk\n- `loader/finder/`: File system scanning to find plugin.json files\n- `sources/`: Plugin sources (bundled, marketplace, etc.)\n\n**Plugin Routing**:\n- External datasources route requests through `pkg/api/pluginproxy/pluginproxy.go`\n- Routes defined in `plugin.json` with HTTP method and path matching (pluginproxy.go:61-93)\n\n## 4. Dashboard Provisioning Pipeline\n\n### Provisioning Flow\nDashboards are provisioned through YAML configuration files. The flow is:\n\n**1. Configuration Loading**\n- Config location: `provisioning/dashboards/*.yml` (from `Cfg.ProvisioningPath`)\n- Read by `pkg/services/provisioning/dashboards/config_reader.go:cfgReader.readConfig()`\n- Parses config files to `config` struct with source definitions\n\n**2. File Discovery**\n- `dashboards/file_reader.go`: Walks disk to find dashboard JSON files\n- Monitors configured directories for changes\n- Supports symlinks and local file paths\n\n**3. Dashboard Sync to Database**\n- `dashboards/dashboard.go:Provisioner.Provision()` (lines 69-87):\n  1. Calls `reader.walkDisk()` to scan files\n  2. Validates dashboards for duplicates\n  3. Calls `provisioner.SaveDashboard()` via `DashboardProvisioningService`\n- Dashboards persisted to `dashboard` table in database\n\n**4. Polling for Changes**\n- `provisioning.go:Run()` (lines 184-218) runs in background\n- Calls `dashboardProvisioner.PollChanges()` periodically\n- Detects file modifications and re-provisions if allowed\n\n### ProvisioningService Interface\nLocated in `pkg/services/provisioning/provisioning.go:ProvisioningService` (lines 100-109):\n```go\ntype ProvisioningService interface {\n    registry.BackgroundService\n    RunInitProvisioners(ctx context.Context) error      // Runs on startup\n    ProvisionDatasources(ctx context.Context) error\n    ProvisionPlugins(ctx context.Context) error\n    ProvisionDashboards(ctx context.Context) error\n    ProvisionAlerting(ctx context.Context) error\n}\n```\n\n### Configuration Storage\n- **In-Memory**: `dashboard_provisioner` tracks which dashboards are provisioned\n- **Database**: Dashboards stored with provisioner name and updated timestamp\n- **Cleanup**: `CleanUpOrphanedDashboards()` removes dashboards when provisioners are removed\n\n## 5. Frontend Build System\n\n### Framework and Tools\n- **Framework**: React with TypeScript\n- **Build Tool**: Webpack\n  - Production build: `scripts/webpack/webpack.prod.js`\n  - Development build: `scripts/webpack/webpack.dev.js`\n- **Package Manager**: Yarn (with Lerna workspaces and NX monorepo)\n- **Monorepo**: Managed by NX and Lerna for multi-package coordination\n\n### Frontend Organization\n\n**Main Entry Point**:\n- `public/app/index.ts` (lines 1-35): Webpack entry point\n- Sets up public path, initializes mock API if needed\n- Imports and calls `app.init()` from `public/app/app.ts`\n\n**Directory Structure**:\n```\npublic/app/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 core/              # Core application logic (routing, services)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 features/          # Feature modules (dashboards, datasources, etc.)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 plugins/           # Plugin loading and management\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 store/             # Redux store (state management)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 types/             # TypeScript type definitions\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 angular/           # Angular-to-React bridge (legacy)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 partials/          # Static HTML templates\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 routes/            # Frontend route definitions\n```\n\n**Packages (Monorepo)**:\nLocated in `packages/` directory, key packages:\n- `@grafana/data`: Core data models and utilities\n- `@grafana/ui`: Shared UI components\n- `@grafana/runtime`: Runtime utilities and APIs\n- `@grafana/schema`: Data model schemas\n- `@grafana/prometheus`: Prometheus query builder\n- `@grafana/sql`: SQL query builder\n\n### Build Commands\nFrom `package.json` (lines 8-66):\n```json\n\"build\": \"NODE_ENV=production nx exec -- webpack --config scripts/webpack/webpack.prod.js\"\n\"dev\": \"NODE_ENV=dev nx exec -- webpack --config scripts/webpack/webpack.dev.js\"\n\"start\": \"NODE_ENV=dev nx exec -- webpack --config scripts/webpack/webpack.dev.js --watch\"\n\"packages:build\": \"nx run-many -t build --projects='@grafana/*'\"\n```\n\n**NX Monorepo Workspace**:\n- Central `nx.json` configures build tasks\n- Each package has `project.json` with build targets\n- Parallel execution via `nx run-many -t build`\n\n## 6. Extension: Adding a New Panel Plugin\n\n### Steps to Create a Panel Plugin\n\n**1. Define Plugin Structure**\n- Create directory: `plugins-bundled/` or external location\n- Create `plugin.json` with:\n  ```json\n  {\n    \"id\": \"my-panel-plugin\",\n    \"type\": \"panel\",\n    \"name\": \"My Panel\",\n    \"info\": { \"version\": \"1.0.0\" },\n    \"dependencies\": { \"grafanaVersion\": \"11.4.0\" }\n  }\n  ```\n- Implement `module.ts` as React component\n\n**2. Frontend Component**\n- Export React component implementing panel interface\n- Component receives props: `options`, `data`, `width`, `height`\n- Register in `module.ts` as a panel type\n\n**3. Plugin Registration**\n- Frontend discovers panels at runtime from plugin metadata\n- Panel registry in `pkg/services/pluginsintegration/` loads from `plugin.json`\n- Plugin appears in \"Choose visualization\" dropdown\n\n**4. Backend Support (if needed)**\n- Implement `backend.QueryDataHandler` in Go if custom query logic needed\n- Create service in `pkg/tsdb/` (following Prometheus pattern)\n- Register in Wire dependency injection (`pkg/server/wire.go`)\n\n**5. Build Process**\n- For bundled panels:\n  - Add to `plugins-bundled/`\n  - Build via `yarn plugins:build` (uses NX)\n  - Compiled into Grafana binary\n- For external plugins:\n  - Use `@grafana/create-plugin` scaffold\n  - Install in Grafana's plugins directory\n  - Loaded via plugin manager at startup\n\n### Plugin Discovery Mechanism\n1. **Disk Scan**: `pkg/plugins/manager/loader/finder/` scans plugin directories\n2. **Validation**: `plugins.go` validates `plugin.json` (lines 35-100)\n3. **Registration**: Registry stores in `pkg/plugins/manager/registry/in_memory.go`\n4. **Frontend Loading**: HTTP API `GET /api/plugins` returns plugin list for UI\n\n### Key Files for Panel Development\n- Frontend: `public/app/plugins/` (existing panel implementations for reference)\n- Backend: `pkg/tsdb/grafana-testdata-datasource/` (example backend plugin)\n- SDK: Use `@grafana/data` and `@grafana/ui` packages from monorepo\n",

Datasource Plugin Architecture\n\n### Plugin System Overview\nGrafana supports two types of plugins:\n1. **Built-in datasources**: Compiled into the binary (under `pkg/tsdb/`)\n2. **Plugin datasources**: External processes communicating via gRPC or HTTP\n\n### Plugin Structure\n**Plugin Metadata** (`plugin.json`):\n- Located in `pkg/plugins/plugins.go:JSONData` (lines 87-100)\n- Defines plugin ID, type, name, category, and routing\n\n**Plugin Registry**:\n- Located in `pkg/plugins/manager/registry/in_memory.go`\n- In-memory registry stores all loaded plugins\n- Plugins registered via `registry.Add()` (lines 45-58)\n- Query plugins via `registry.Plugin()` (lines 29-31)\n\n### Backend Plugin Communication\n**grafana-plugin-sdk-go**:\n- Grafana uses `github.com/grafana/grafana-plugin-sdk-go/backend` interface\n- Built-in datasources implement these handlers:\n  - `QueryDataHandler`: Execute queries\n  - `CheckHealthHandler`: Health checks\n  - `CallResourceHandler`: Custom resource endpoints\n  - `AdmissionHandler`: Validate/mutate objects\n  - `StreamHandler`: Real-time streaming\n  - `CollectMetricsHandler`: Prometheus metrics\n\n**Example: Prometheus Datasource** (`pkg/tsdb/prometheus/prometheus.go`):\n```go\nfunc (s *Service) QueryData(ctx context.Context, req *backend.QueryDataRequest) (*backend.QueryDataResponse, error)\nfunc (s *Service) CheckHealth(ctx context.Context, req *backend.CheckHealthRequest) (*backend.CheckHealthResult, error)\n```\n\n### Plugin Loading\n**Plugin Manager**: `pkg/plugins/manager/`\n- `loader/loader.go`: Discovers and loads plugins from disk\n- `loader/finder/`: File system scanning to find plugin.json files\n- `sources/`: Plugin sources (bundled, marketplace, etc.)\n\n**Plugin Routing**:\n- External datasources route requests through `pkg/api/pluginproxy/pluginproxy.go`\n- Routes defined in `plugin.json` with HTTP method and path matching (pluginproxy.go:61-93)\n\n## 4. Dashboard Provisioning Pipeline\n\n### Provisioning Flow\nDashboards are provisioned through YAML configuration files. The flow is:\n\n**1. Configuration Loading**\n- Config location: `provisioning/dashboards/*.yml` (from `Cfg.ProvisioningPath`)\n- Read by `pkg/services/provisioning/dashboards/config_reader.go:cfgReader.readConfig()`\n- Parses config files to `config` struct with source definitions\n\n**2. File Discovery**\n- `dashboards/file_reader.go`: Walks disk to find dashboard JSON files\n- Monitors configured directories for changes\n- Supports symlinks and local file paths\n\n**3. Dashboard Sync to Database**\n- `dashboards/dashboard.go:Provisioner.Provision()` (lines 69-87):\n  1. Calls `reader.walkDisk()` to scan files\n  2. Validates dashboards for duplicates\n  3. Calls `provisioner.SaveDashboard()` via `DashboardProvisioningService`\n- Dashboards persisted to `dashboard` table in database\n\n**4. Polling for Changes**\n- `provisioning.go:Run()` (lines 184-218) runs in background\n- Calls `dashboardProvisioner.PollChanges()` periodically\n- Detects file modifications and re-provisions if allowed\n\n### ProvisioningService Interface\nLocated in `pkg/services/provisioning/provisioning.go:ProvisioningService` (lines 100-109):\n```go\ntype ProvisioningService interface {\n    registry.BackgroundService\n    RunInitProvisioners(ctx context.Context) error      // Runs on startup\n    ProvisionDatasources(ctx context.Context) error\n    ProvisionPlugins(ctx context.Context) error\n    ProvisionDashboards(ctx context.Context) error\n    ProvisionAlerting(ctx context.Context) error\n}\n```\n\n### Configuration Storage\n- **In-Memory**: `dashboard_provisioner` tracks which dashboards are provisioned\n- **Database**: Dashboards stored with provisioner name and updated timestamp\n- **Cleanup**: `CleanUpOrphanedDashboards()` removes dashboards when provisioners are removed\n\n## 5. # Grafana Codebase Architecture Onboarding

## 1. Main Entry Points

### Binary Entry Point
The main Grafana server binary is built from `pkg/cmd/grafana/main.go` (lines 23-31). The application uses the **urfave/cli v2** framework for command-line parsing and routing.

**Bootstrap Flow:**
1. The grafana-server command delegates to the main `grafana` binary via `pkg/util/cmd/cmd.go:RunGrafanaCmd()` (lines 15-74)
2. The main CLI app is created in `pkg/cmd/grafana/main.go:MainApp()` (lines 34-73), which registers two CLI commands:
   - `CLICommand`: For grafana-cli utilities
   - `ServerCommand`: For starting the server

3. The server command is defined in `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go:ServerCommand()` (lines 28-44)
4. The `RunServer()` function (lines 46-125) performs the bootstrap:
   - Reads configuration from `setting.NewCfgFromArgs()` (lines 96-101)
   - Initializes profiling and tracing (lines 71-76)
   - Calls `server.Initialize()` from `pkg/server/server.go` (lines 108-120)
   - Sets up signal handling for graceful shutdown (line 123)
   - Runs the HTTP server (line 124)

### Service Initialization
The `server.Initialize()` function uses **Google Wire** dependency injection (defined in `pkg/server/wire.go`) to instantiate all core services. The Wire configuration includes 50+ services covering APIs, datasources, authentication, provisioning, and more (wire.go lines 39-443).

- **Location**: `pkg/api/api.go` (HTTP routes registered at line 55)
- **Responsibility**: Defines REST API endpoints, middleware, and request handlers
- **Key Files**:
  - `http_server.go`: HTTPServer struct and initializati
